    I am amending this statement as it was made in TOD to the more comprehensive term misthological life in the
Heavenly City rather than mere millennial life in the millennial city. This is more consistent with the fact that the rewards
and city are eternal and with the fact that Abraham was looking for a heavenly city (Heb 11:10,16), not a millennial city,
which God had prepared as a reward for him and others like him. Abraham would have been shocked by Chitwood’s
proposal that his sacrifice of Isaac would be misthologically meaningless after 1000 years and that all believers are
allegedly given access to the Heavenly City for all eternity. Abraham rightly would recoil from such misthology. Unlike
Chitwood, with his over-refined millennial distinctions, Abraham was looking for an eternal reward. Also, I am splitting
Rev 3:5 between categories three and four, the first reference to name (onoma) in that verse now falling into category
three, while the second usage remains in category four. Additionally, Rev 21:27 should probably be considered as
operating functionally in the third category, not the fourth. This verse implements a soteric-mistholic (or mistholic-
soteric) antithetical juxtaposition in which believers who qualify morally to enter by the gates into the city are contrasted
with immoral unbelievers outside the city. This verse is not a simple soteriological contrast. I charted it correctly in TOD
(p. 106) but possibly posed a false dichotomy between the soteric and mistholic possibilities (p. 1060, n. 919). I am now
inclined to see Rev 21:27 as operating in both capacities, but primarily in the misthological category. Only, but not all,
of those names who are recorded soteriologically in the LBOL will enter the city. Alternatively, the LBOL may be a
strictly misthological record. In any case, only those names who are recorded misthologically will enter the city by gates,
that is, have a glorified entrance. Visitors to the city who are born in the eternal state may or may not have their names
recorded soteriologically.
128
    Posing a soteric-mistholic dualism for some of these passages is a new development derived from Misthological
Models.
129
    In MMP2 I argue that the promise of not erasing their names from the BOL in Rev 3:5b is being used in a dual
capacity. In MMP4 I expand that duality within this list to include other passages. Additionally, MMP1 and MMP3
present evidence that the transformation in Phil 3:21 is dualistically soteric-mistholic (or perhaps we should say
mistholic-soteric).
Page 110                                                                                                Rewards are Eternal

Similarly, the citizenship within Heaven affirmed in Phil 3:20 probably includes the eschatological destruction of
unfaithful believers, alluded to in Phil 3:19 (cp. 1:15-16; 2:21), within its scope of possibilities, thus providing the impetus
for the moral exhortation to stand firm in the Lord in Phil 4:1.
        An exclusively soteric citizenship makes little sense as a grounds for appealing for moral performance in a context
of misthological destruction. The telic (telos) destruction of these particular heavenly citizens in Philippians gives
grounds for concluding that their names will be erased from the heavenly registry. They will reap misthological
destruction (lose misthological life) rather than gain misthological life. Citizenship suggests membership in a city. For
that matter, Govett would translate politeuma as city in Phil 3:20 and, like many other commentators, believes that Paul
is describing the Lord as coming from this city.130 In Phil 1:27 and 3:20 respectively, Paul exhorts us to act as members
of this heavenly city (politeuo) in view of our membership in that city (politeuma). This city is the literal city of New
Jerusalem. In terms of contingency and unrealized potentiality, their names can be erased from the heavenly registry,
thereby excluding them from residency in the Heavenly City. Paul is making explicit what John made implicit in Rev 3:5.
The names of unfaithful believers will be erased from the city register so that they lose their citizenship in this heavenly
city and thus experience misthological destruction. The names of those whose names will remain in the heavenly registry
are the “church of the firstborn who are registered in heaven” (Heb 12:23; NKJ).
                                                   Conclusion
       This discussion has evaluated two opposing propositions concerning rewards. The temporary reward (TR)
position was pitted against the eternal reward (ER) proposition. Likewise, two rudimentary propositions were posed
regarding the Book of Life (BOL). The single book hypothesis (SBH) was compared to the multiple book hypothesis
(MBH). Structurally, this comparison gave two basic ways to pose a TR position: TR-SBH or TR-MBH. Summarily, two
primary options were entertained for the ER position: ER-SBH or ER-MBH.131
                                              Illustration 69. SBH and MBH
                                                       SBH           MBH
                                               TR     TR-SBH        TR-MBH
                                               ER     ER-SBH        ER-MBH

        The basic choices can be displayed in a grid of two columns (SBH and MBH) and two rows (TR and ER). If the
SBH is adopted per the first column, then the ER position is far superior to the TR position in that ER-SBH does not
pose that names written from the foundation of the world, and thus seemingly written permanently, are temporarily
erased. Also, ER-SBH does not confuse gift with a reward by turning the reward into a gift or the gift into a reward. ER-
SBH is also far less convoluted in terms of necessary inferences. Thus Occam’s Razor would favor ER-SBH over TR-
SBH. If one adopts the SBH, then one should adopt ER-SBH.
        Similarly, if MBH is adopted in preference for the second column, then Occam’s Razor favors ER-SBH over TR-
SBH. Even though Occam’s Razor might favor Chitwood’s TR-SBH over the TR-SBH model of Faust in some ways,
Chitwood’s citations and arguments were even more strained than those of Faust on several accounts. But this only pits
one TR model against another TR model. These offsetting TR models demonstrate a strain even when simply compared
to one another, much less when pitted against the superior ER options. In contrast, the problem for the ER camp is in
trying to decide which ER-MBH model is best. Several excellent candidates were put forth. The arguments for each ER
model are internally consistent. No strain is imposed upon the text. At the very least, three ER-MBH models were found
to be worthy of consideration. Moreover, these models complement and reinforce one another to such an extent that
postulation is possible that all three models are intended by the data. What is more, a multiple column hypothesis (MCH),
in the form of a Book of Life Spreadsheet (BOLS), might be just as suitable for the ER position as is the multiple book
hypothesis (MBH). When it comes to the multiple entry format, whether it be MBH or MCH, TR flounders while ER
flourishes.




130
  Govett, Romans, 472.
131
  The acronyms respectively refer to: Eternal Rewards—Singular Book Hypothesis (ER-SBH) and Eternal Rewards—
Multiple Book Hypothesis (ER-MBH).
Excursus on the Book of Life                                                                                 Page 111
                                       Illustration 70. Sequence of the Books




       In WWWS, I postulated that the Book of Life (BOL) was a soteriological book, thus completely distinct from the
Books of Works (BOW). Therefore, I object to Chitwood’s making the BOL one of the BOW. I also presented a
rudimentary argument for the Book for Life (BFL). In subsequent reflections within MMP2 and MMP4, I theorized that
this multiple book hypothesis is logically necessary and exegetically feasible and referred to the BFL as a Bema Book.
Conceptually, my conclusions may be pictured rather easily with the sequence illustration. The BOL is consulted
soteriologically in order to determine if one is allowed into the kingdom or cast into the Lake of Fire. The BOW are
consulted to determine the degree of one’s reward/punishment in the kingdom or Lake of Fire. The BFL is a record of
those believers who will achieve a degree of reward sufficient to rule in the kingdom and live in the Reward City.
       More complex considerations come into play when moving beyond this simple topical summary to engage the
texts exegetically. The Principle of Duality (POD) allows postulation that the texts are used in a dual capacities. The
Book of Life Spreadsheet (BOLS) is the illustration used in the present work to accommodate this more complex vantage
point. See BOL in SML for another illustration used to interact with that more complex discussion in MMP2.
                                   Illustration 71. Revised Sequence of the Books
Page 112                                                                                             Rewards are Eternal

       Alternatively, Chitwood and Hollandsworth both pose, to some degree at least, a dichotomy between the BOL and
the Lamb’s Book of Life (LBOL). Chitwood takes the BOL as misthological and the LBOL as soteriological. Inversely
to Chitwood’s take on the LBOL and as a mediation between Chitwood and me regarding the BOL, Hollandsworth
proposes that the LBOL is misthological but the BOL is dualistic: soteriological and misthological. His approach is far
superior to Chitwood’s proposal. If the MBH is adopted and the POD is not applied to the LBOL, then the LBOL should
be taken misthologically, not soteriologically, just as Hollandsworth has proposed. Chitwood got it backwards. As to
Hollandsworth’s mediation, in contrast to my applying POD to both the BOL and LBOL, Hollandsworth applies POD
only to the BOL. His proposition is attractive and makes a good competing model to my own. Indeed, our models are
complementary if multiple vantage points are allowed.
       In any event, in deference to Hollandsworth’s postulation, I have modified my original illustration for the sequence
of books to allow Hollandsworth’s winsome vantage point regarding the LBOL. For simplicity’s sake, I am still picturing
the BOL simply as soteriological in the illustration. The more complex consideration, that the BOL is used in a dual
capacity, is hinted at only subtly by the fact that the BOL is much thicker than the LBOL. The LBOL is the resulting list
of names not erased misthologically from the BOL by the BOW. Thus, BOL serves subtly in a dual capacity. The issue
of erasure is strictly misthological. Pertaining to how the BOL is used in Revelation, names are not erased
soteriologically, only misthologically, from the BOL.
       Soteriologically, the names of all believers are written eternally and permanently, from the foundation of the world,
in the BOL. Misthologically, the names of all overcomers are written eternally and permanently, from the foundation of
the world, in the LBOL. The latter is a smaller subset of the former. Not all believers are overcomers in the misthological
sense. The Scripture purposefully indicates that overcomers compose a smaller subset of believers when it hints that only
the names of overcomers would not be erased misthologically from the list of believers. This adaptation of
Hollandsworth’s model is very attractive. Therefore, a verity of suitable models depict the ER position. In this revised
adaptation of Hollandsworth’s model, the LBOL in Rev 21:27 is an explicit affirmation that rewards continue in the
eternal state and are limited to the faithful subset, namely overcomers. Hence, rewards are eternal.
